22→)\n    23→\n    24→func prepareFinalInputVariableValue(addr addrs.AbsInputVariableInstance, raw *InputValue, cfg *configs.Variable) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n    25→\tvar diags Changing the ephemerality of an\n   198→\t\t// input variable is a breaking change to a module's API.\n   199→\t\tval = val.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n   200→\t} else {\n   201→\t\tif marks.Contains(val, marks.Ephemeral) {\n   202→\t\t\tvar subject hcl.Range\n   203→\t\t\tif raw.HasSourceRange() {\n   204→\t\t\t\tsubject = raw.SourceRange.ToHCL()\n   205→\t\t\t} else {\n   206→\t\t\t\t// We shouldn't typically get here for ephemeral values, because\n   207→\t\t\t\t// all of the source types that can represent expressions that\n   208→\t\t\t\t// could potentially produce ephemeral values are those which\n   209→\t\t\t\t// have source locations. ct != 0 {\n   243→\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"check state says that %s should have no rules, but it has %d\", addr, ct))\n   244→\t\t}\n   245→\t\treturn diags\n   246→\t}\n   247→\n   248→\t// We'll build just one evaluation context covering the data needed by\n   249→\t// all of the rules together, since that'll minimize lock contention\n   250→\t// on the state, plan, etc.\n   251→\tscope := ctx.EvaluationScope(nil, nil, EvalDataForNoInstanceKey)\n   252→\tvar refs []*addrs.Reference\n   253→\tfor _, rule := range rules {\n   254→\t\tcondRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.Condition)\n   255→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   256→\t\tmsgRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.ErrorMessage)\n   257→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   258→\t\trefs = append(refs, condRefs...)\n   259→\t\trefs = append(refs, msgRefs...)\n   260→\t}\n   261→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   262→\t\t// If any of the references were invalid then evaluating the expressions\n   263→\t\t// will duplicate those errors, so we'll bail out early.\n   264→\t\treturn diags\n   265→\t}\n   266→\thclCtx, moreDiags := scope.EvalContext(refs)\n   267→\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   268→\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n   269→\t\treturn diags\n   270→\t}\n   271→\n   272→\t// HACK: Historically we manually built a very constrained hcl.EvalContext\n   273→\t// here, which only included the value of the one specific input variable\n   274→\t// we're validating, since we didn't yet support referring to anything\n   275→\t// else. That accidentally bypassed our rule that input variables are\n   276→\t// always unknown during the validate walk, and thus accidentally created\n   277→\t// a useful behavior of actually checking constant-only values against\n   278→\t// their validation rules just during \"terraform validate\", rather than\n   279→\t// having to run \"terraform plan\".\n   280→\t//\n   281→\t// Although that behavior was accidental, it makes simple validation rules\n   282→\t// more useful and is protected by compatibility promises, and so we'll\n   283→\t// fake it here by overwriting the unknown value that scope.EvalContext\n   284→\t// will have inserted with a possibly-more-known value using the same\n   285→\t// strategy our special code used to use.\n   286→\tourVal := ctx.NamedValues().GetInputVariableValue(addr)\n   287→\tif ourVal != cty.NilVal {\n   288→\t\t// (it would be weird for ourVal to be nil here, but we'll tolerate it\n   289→\t\t// because it was scope.EvalContext's responsibility to check for the\n   290→\t\t// absent final value, and even if it didn't we'll just get an\n   291→\t\t// evaluation error when evaluating the expressions below anyway.)\n   292→\n   293→\t\t// Our goal here is to make sure that a reference to the variable\n   294→\t\t// we're checking will evaluate to ourVal, regardless of what else\n   295→\t\t// scope.EvalContext might have put in the variables table.\n   296→\t\tif hclCtx.Variables == nil {\n   297→\t\t\thclCtx.Variables = make(map[string]cty.Value)\n   298→\t\t}\n   299→\t\tif varsVal, ok := hclCtx.Variables[\"var\"]; Due to an implementation quirk, all prior versions of\n   338→\t// Terraform would treat error messages specified using JSON\n   339→\t// configuration syntax (.tf.json) as string literals, even if they\n   340→\t// contained the \"${\" template expression operator. As we add support for error message expressions, we are\n   347→\t// unable to perfectly distinguish between these two cases.\n   348→\t//\n   349→\t// To ensure that we don't break backwards compatibility, we have the\n   350→\t// below fallback logic if the error message fails to evaluate. This\n   351→\t// should only have any effect for JSON configurations. The gohcl\n   352→\t// DecodeExpression function behaves differently when the source of the\n   353→\t// expression is a JSON configuration file and a nil context is passed.\n   354→\tif errorDiags.HasErrors() {\n   355→\t\t// Attempt to decode the expression as a string literal. Passing\n   356→\t\t// nil as the context forces a JSON syntax string value to be\n   357→\t\t// interpreted as a string literal.\n   358→\t\tvar errorString string\n   359→\t\tmoreErrorDiags := gohcl.DecodeExpression(validation.ErrorMessage, nil, &errorString)\n   360→\t\tif !moreErrorDiags.HasErrors() {\n   361→\t\t\t// Decoding succeeded, meaning that this is a JSON syntax\n   362→\t\t\t// string value. Please file a GitHub issue if this would break your workflow.\\n\\n%s\", errorDiags.Error()),\n   374→\t\t\t\t\tSubject:     validation.ErrorMessage.Range().Ptr(),\n   375→\t\t\t\t\tContext: 389→\t}\n   390→\tif !result.IsKnown() {\n   391→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s rule %s condition value is unknown, so skipping validation for now\", addr, validation.DeclRange)\n   392→\n   393→\t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusUnknown}, diags // We'll wait until we've learned more, then.\n   394→\t}\n   395→\tif result.IsNull() {\n   396→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   397→\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n   398→\t\t\tSummary:     errInvalidCondition,\n   399→\t\t\tDetail:      \"Validation condition expression We do not apply defaults to top-level\n\t// null values, as doing so could prevent assigning null to a nullable\n\t// variable.\n\tif cfg.TypeDefaults != nil && !given.IsNull() {\n\t\tgiven = cfg.TypeDefaults.Apply(given)\n\t}\n\n\tval, err := convert.Convert(given, convertTy)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s has unsuitable type\\n  got:  %s\\n  want: %s\", addr, given.Type(), convertTy)\n\t\tvar detail string\n\t\tvar subject *hcl.Range\n\t\tif nonFileSource != \"\" {\n\t\t\tdetail = fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\"Unsuitable value for %s %s: %s.\",\n\t\t\t\taddr, nonFileSource, err,\n\t\t\t)\n\t\t\tsubject = cfg.DeclRange.Ptr()\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tdetail = fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\"The given value is not suitable for %s declared at %s: %s.\",\n\t\t\t\taddr, cfg.DeclRange.String(), err,\n\t\t\t)\n\t\t\tsubject = sourceRange.ToHCL().Ptr()\n\n\t\t\t// In some workflows, the operator running terraform does not have access to the variables\n\t\t\t// themselves. They are for example stored in encrypted files that will be used by the CI toolset\n\t\t\t// and not by the operator directly. In such a case, the failing secret value should not be\n\t\t\t// displayed to the operator\n\t\t\tif cfg.Sensitive {\n\t\t\t\tdetail = fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\t\"The given value is not suitable for %s, which is sensitive: %s. Invalid value defined at %s.\",\n\t\t\t\t\taddr, err, sourceRange.ToHCL(),\n\t\t\t\t)\n\t\t\t\tsubject = cfg.DeclRange.Ptr()\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid value for input variable\",\n\t\t\tDetail:   detail,\n\t\t\tSubject:  subject,\n\t\t})\n\t\t// We'll return a placeholder unknown value to avoid producing\n\t\t// redundant downstream errors.\n\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cfg.Type), diags\n\t}\n\n\t// By the time we get here, we know:\n\t// - val matches the variable's type constraint\n\t// - val is definitely not cty.NilVal, but might be a null value if the given was already null.\n\t//\n\t// That means we just need to handle the case where the value is null,\n\t// which might mean we need to use the default value, or produce an error.\n\t//\n\t// For historical reasons we do this only for a \"non-nullable\" variable.\n\t// Nullable variables just appear as null if they were set to null,\n\t// regardless of any default value.\n\tif val.IsNull() && !cfg.Nullable {\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s is defined as null\", addr)\n\t\tif defaultVal != cty.NilVal {\n\t\t\tval = defaultVal\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s is non-nullable but set to null, and is required\", addr)\n\t\t\tif nonFileSource != \"\" {\n\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Required variable not set`,\n\t\t\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\"Unsuitable value for %s %s: required variable may not be set to null.\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\taddr, nonFileSource,\n\t\t\t\t\t),\n\t\t\t\t\tSubject: cfg.DeclRange.Ptr(),\n\t\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Required variable not set`,\n\t\t\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\"The given value is not suitable for %s defined at %s: required variable may not be set to null.\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\taddr, cfg.DeclRange.String(),\n\t\t\t\t\t),\n\t\t\t\t\tSubject: sourceRange.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t// Stub out our return value so that the semantic checker doesn't\n\t\t\t// produce redundant downstream errors.\n\t\t\tval = cty.UnknownVal(cfg.Type)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tif !cfg.Ephemeral {\n\t\t// An ephemeral input variable always has an ephemeral value inside the\n\t\t// module, even if the value assigned to it from outside is not. This\n\t\t// is a useful simplification so that module authors can be explicit\n\t\t// about what guarantees they are intending to make (regardless of\n\t\t// current implementation details). Changing the ephemerality of an\n\t\t// input variable is a breaking change to a module's API.\n\t\tval = val.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n\t} else {\n\t\tif marks.Contains(val, marks.Ephemeral) {\n\t\t\tvar subject hcl.Range\n\t\t\tif raw.HasSourceRange() {\n\t\t\t\tsubject = raw.SourceRange.ToHCL()\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t// We shouldn't typically get here for ephemeral values, because\n\t\t\t\t// all of the source types that can represent expressions that\n\t\t\t\t// could potentially produce ephemeral values are those which\n\t\t\t\t// have source locations. This is just here for robustness.\n\t\t\t\tsubject = cfg.DeclRange\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Ephemeral value not allowed\",\n\t\t\t\tDetail:   \"This input variable is not declared as accepting a ephemeral values, so it cannot be set to a result derived from an ephemeral value.\",\n\t\t\t\tSubject:  subject.Ptr(),\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn val, diags\n}\n\n// evalVariableValidations ensures that all of the configured custom validations\n// for a variable are passing.\n//\n// This must be used only after any side-effects that make the value of the\n// variable available for use in expression evaluation, such as\n// EvalModuleCallArgument for variables in descendant modules.\nfunc evalVariableValidations(addr addrs.AbsInputVariableInstance, ctx EvalContext, rules []*configs.CheckRule, valueRng hcl.Range, validateWalk bool) (diags tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tif len(rules) == 0 {\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: no validation rules declared for %s, so skipping\", addr)\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: validating %s\", addr)\n\n\tcheckState := ctx.Checks()\n\tif !checkState.ConfigHasChecks(addr.ConfigCheckable()) {\n\t\t// We have nothing to do if this object doesn't have any checks,\n\t\t// but the \"rules\" slice should agree that we don't.\n\t\tif ct := len(rules); ct != 0 {\n\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"check state says that %s should have no rules, but it has %d\", addr, ct))\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn diags\n\t}\n\n\t// We'll build just one evaluation context covering the data needed by\n\t// all of the rules together, since that'll minimize lock contention\n\t// on the state, plan, etc.\n\tscope := ctx.EvaluationScope(nil, nil, EvalDataForNoInstanceKey)\n\tvar refs []*addrs.Reference\n\tfor _, rule := range rules {\n\t\tcondRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.Condition)\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\t\tmsgRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.ErrorMessage)\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\t\trefs = append(refs, condRefs...)\n\t\trefs = append(refs, msgRefs...)\n\t}\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t// If any of the references were invalid then evaluating the expressions\n\t\t// will duplicate those errors, so we'll bail out early.\n\t\treturn diags\n\t}\n\thclCtx, moreDiags := scope.EvalContext(refs)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn diags\n\t}\n\n\t// HACK: Historically we manually built a very constrained hcl.EvalContext\n\t// here, which only included the value of the one specific input variable\n\t// we're validating, since we didn't yet support referring to anything\n\t// else. That accidentally bypassed our rule that input variables are\n\t// always unknown during the validate walk, and thus accidentally created\n\t// a useful behavior of actually checking constant-only values against\n\t// their validation rules just during \"terraform validate\", rather than\n\t// having to run \"terraform plan\".\n\t//\n\t// Although that behavior was accidental, it makes simple validation rules\n\t// more useful and is protected by compatibility promises, and so we'll\n\t// fake it here by overwriting the unknown value that scope.EvalContext\n\t// will have inserted with a possibly-more-known value using the same\n\t// strategy our special code used to use.\n\tourVal := ctx.NamedValues().GetInputVariableValue(addr)\n\tif ourVal != cty.NilVal {\n\t\t// (it would be weird for ourVal to be nil here, but we'll tolerate it\n\t\t// because it was scope.EvalContext's responsibility to check for the\n\t\t// absent final value, and even if it didn't we'll just get an\n\t\t// evaluation error when evaluating the expressions below anyway.)\n\n\t\t// Our goal here is to make sure that a reference to the variable\n\t\t// we're checking will evaluate to ourVal, regardless of what else\n\t\t// scope.EvalContext might have put in the variables table.\n\t\tif hclCtx.Variables == nil {\n\t\t\thclCtx.Variables = make(map[string]cty.Value)\n\t\t}\n\t\tif varsVal, ok := hclCtx.Variables[\"var\"]; ok {\n\t\t\t// Unfortunately we need to unpack and repack the object here,\n\t\t\t// because cty values are immutable.\n\t\t\tattrs := varsVal.AsValueMap()\n\t\t\tattrs[addr.Variable.Name] = ourVal\n\t\t\thclCtx.Variables[\"var\"] = cty.ObjectVal(attrs)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\thclCtx.Variables[\"var\"] = cty.ObjectVal(map[string]cty.Value{\n\t\t\t\taddr.Variable.Name: ourVal,\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tfor ix, validation := range rules {\n\t\tresult, ruleDiags := evalVariableValidation(validation, hclCtx, valueRng, addr, ix, validateWalk)\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(ruleDiags)\n\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s status is now %s\", addr, result.Status)\n\t\tif result.Status == checks.StatusFail {\n\t\t\tcheckState.ReportCheckFailure(addr, addrs.InputValidation, ix, result.FailureMessage)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tcheckState.ReportCheckResult(addr, addrs.InputValidation, ix, result.Status)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn diags\n}\n\nfunc evalVariableValidation(validation *configs.CheckRule, hclCtx *hcl.EvalContext, valueRng hcl.Range, addr addrs.AbsInputVariableInstance, ix int, validateWalk bool) (checkResult, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tconst errInvalidCondition = \"Invalid variable validation result\"\n\tconst errInvalidValue = \"Invalid value for variable\"\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\tresult, moreDiags := validation.Condition.Value(hclCtx)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\terrorValue, errorDiags := validation.ErrorMessage.Value(hclCtx)\n\n\t// The following error handling is a workaround to preserve backwards\n\t// compatibility. Due to an implementation quirk, all prior versions of\n\t// Terraform would treat error messages specified using JSON\n\t// configuration syntax (.tf.json) as string literals, even if they\n\t// contained the \"${\" template expression operator. This behaviour did\n\t// not match that of HCL configuration syntax, where a template\n\t// expression would result in a validation error.\n\t//\n\t// As a result, users writing or generating JSON configuration syntax\n\t// may have specified error messages which are invalid template\n\t// expressions. As we add support for error message expressions, we are\n\t// unable to perfectly distinguish between these two cases.\n\t//\n\t// To ensure that we don't break backwards compatibility, we have the\n\t// below fallback logic if the error message fails to evaluate. This\n\t// should only have any effect for JSON configurations. The gohcl\n\t// DecodeExpression function behaves differently when the source of the\n\t// expression is a JSON configuration file and a nil context is passed.\n\tif errorDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t// Attempt to decode the expression as a string literal. We rewrap that as a cty value to allow later\n\t\t\t// decoding to succeed.\n\t\t\terrorValue = cty.StringVal(errorString)\n\n\t\t\t// This warning diagnostic explains this odd behaviour, while\n\t\t\t// giving us an escape hatch to change this to a hard failure\n\t\t\t// in some future Terraform 1.x version.\n\t\t\terrorDiags = hcl.Diagnostics{\n\t\t\t\t&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagWarning,\n\t\t\t\t\tSummary:     \"Validation error message expression is invalid\",\n\t\t\t\t\tDetail:      fmt.Sprintf(\"The error message provided could not be evaluated as an expression, so Terraform is interpreting it as a string literal.\\n\\nIn future versions of Terraform, this will be considered an error. Please file a GitHub issue if this would break your workflow.\\n\\n%s\", errorDiags.Error()),\n\t\t\t\t\tSubject:     validation.ErrorMessage.Range().Ptr(),\n\t\t\t\t\tContext:     validation.DeclRange.Ptr(),\n\t\t\t\t\tExpression:  validation.ErrorMessage,\n\t\t\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n\t\t\t\t},\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// We want to either report the original diagnostics if %s rule %s check rule evaluation failed: %s\", addr, validation.DeclRange, diags.Err().Error())\n\t}\n\tif !result.IsKnown() {\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s rule %s condition value is unknown, so skipping validation for now\", addr, validation.DeclRange)\n\n\t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusUnknown}, diags // We'll wait until we've learned more, then.\n\t}\n\tif result.IsNull() {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:     errInvalidCondition,\n\t\t\tDetail:      \"Validation condition expression must return either true or false, not null.\",\n\t\t\tSubject:     validation.Condition.Range().Ptr(),\n\t\t\tExpression:  validation.Condition,\n\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusError}, diags\n\t}\n\tvar err error\n\tresult, err = convert.Convert(result, cty.Bool)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: condition may be marked if the input variable is bound to\n\t// a sensitive value. This is irrelevant to the validation process, so\n\t// we discard the marks now.\n\tresult, _ = result.Unmark()\n\tstatus := checks.StatusForCtyValue(result)\n\n\tif status != checks.StatusFail {\n\t\treturn checkResult{Status: status}, diags\n\t}\n\n\tif !errorValue.IsKnown() {\n\t\tif validateWalk {\n\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] evalVariableValidations: %s rule %s error_message value is unknown, so skipping validation for now\", addr, validation.DeclRange)\n\t\t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusUnknown}, diags\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:     \"Invalid error message\",\n\t\t\tDetail:      \"Unsuitable value for error message: expression refers to values that won't be known until the apply phase.\",\n\t\t\tSubject:     validation.ErrorMessage.Range().Ptr(),\n\t\t\tExpression:  validation.ErrorMessage,\n\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n\t\t\tExtra:       diagnosticCausedByUnknown(true),\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn checkResult{\n\t\t\tStatus: checks.StatusError,\n\t\t}, diags\n\t}\n\n\tvar errorMessage string\n\tif !errorDiags.HasErrors() && !errorValue.IsNull() {\n\t\tvar err error\n\t\terrorValue, err = convert.Convert(errorValue, cty.String)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\tSummary:     \"Invalid error message\",\n\t\t\t\tDetail:      fmt.Sprintf(\"Unsuitable value for error message: %s.\", tfdiags.FormatError(err)),\n\t\t\t\tSubject:     validation.ErrorMessage.Range().Ptr(),\n\t\t\t\tExpression:  validation.ErrorMessage,\n\t\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tif marks.Has(errorValue, marks.Sensitive) {\n\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\n\t\t\t\t\tSummary: \"Error message refers to sensitive values\",\n\t\t\t\t\tDetail: `The error expression used to explain this condition refers to sensitive values. Terraform will not display the resulting message.\n\nYou can correct this by removing references to sensitive values, or by carefully using the nonsensitive() function if the expression will not reveal the sensitive data.`,\n\n\t\t\t\t\tSubject:     validation.ErrorMessage.Range().Ptr(),\n\t\t\t\t\tExpression:  validation.ErrorMessage,\n\t\t\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n\t\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t\terrorMessage = \"The error message included a sensitive value, so it will not be displayed.\"\n\t\t\t} else if marks.Has(errorValue, marks.Ephemeral) {\n\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\n\t\t\t\t\tSummary: \"Error message refers to ephemeral values\",\n\t\t\t\t\tDetail: `The error expression used to explain this condition refers to ephemeral values. See the documentation for the InputValue\n    36→\t// type for more information on how to correctly populate this.\n    37→\t//\n    38→\t// During the apply phase it's only valid to specify values for input\n    39→\t// values that were declared as ephemeral, because all other input\n    40→\t// values must retain the values that were specified during planning.\n    41→\tSetVariables InputValues\n    42→}\n    43→\n    44→// ApplyOpts creates an [ApplyOpts] with copies of all of the elements that\n    45→// are expected to propagate from plan to apply when planning and applying\n    46→// in the same process.\n    47→//\n    48→// In practice planning and applying are often separated into two different\n    49→// executions, in which case callers must retain enough information between\n    50→// plan and apply to construct an equivalent [ApplyOpts] themselves without\n    51→// using this function. This is here mainly for convenient internal use such\n    52→// as in test cases.\n    53→func (po *PlanOpts) ApplyOpts() *ApplyOpts {\n    54→\treturn &ApplyOpts{\n    55→\t\tExternalProviders: po.ExternalProviders,\n    56→\t}\n    57→}\n    58→\n    59→// Apply performs the actions described by the given Plan object and returns\n    60→// the resulting updated state.\n    61→//\n    62→// The given configuration *must* be the same configuration that was passed\n    63→// earlier to Context.Plan in order to create this plan.\n    64→//\n    65→// Even if the returned diagnostics contains errors, Apply always returns the\n    66→// resulting state which is likely to have been partially-updated.\n    67→//\n    68→// The [opts] argument may be nil to indicate that no special options are\n    69→// required. In that case, Apply will use a default set of options. Some\n    70→// options in [PlanOpts] when creating a plan must be echoed with equivalent\n    71→// settings during apply, so leaving opts as nil might not be valid for\n    72→// certain combinations of plan-time options.\n    73→func (c *Context) Apply(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n    74→\tstate, _, diags := c.ApplyAndEval(plan, config, opts)\n    75→\treturn state, diags\n    76→}\n    77→\n    78→// ApplyAndEval is like [Context.Apply] except that it additionally makes a\n    79→// best effort to return a [lang.Scope] which can evaluate expressions in the\n    80→// root module based on the content of the new state.\n    81→//\n    82→// The scope will be nil if the apply process doesn't complete successfully\n    83→// enough to produce a valid evaluation scope. If the returned state is nil\n    84→// then the scope will always be nil, but it's also possible for the scope\n    85→// to be nil even when the state isn't, if the apply didn't complete enough for\n    86→// the evaluation scope to produce consistent results.\n    87→func (c *Context) ApplyAndEval(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n    88→\tdefer c.acquireRun(\"apply\")()\n    89→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n    90→\n    91→\tif plan == nil {\n    92→\t\tpanic(\"cannot apply nil plan\")\n    93→\t}\n    94→\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] Building and walking apply graph for %s plan\", plan.UIMode)\n    95→\n    96→\tif opts == nil {\n    97→\t\topts = &ApplyOpts{}\n    98→\t}\n    99→\n   100→\tif plan.Errored {\n   101→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   102→\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n   103→\t\t\t\"Cannot apply failed plan\",\n   104→\t\t\t`The given plan is incomplete due to errors during planning, and so it cannot be applied.`,\n   105→\t\t))\n   106→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   107→\t}\n   108→\tif !plan.Applyable {\n   109→\t\tif plan.Changes.Empty() {\n   110→\t\t\t// If a plan is not applyable but it didn't have any errors then that\n   111→\t\t\t// suggests it was a \"no-op\" plan, which doesn't really do any\n   112→\t\t\t// harm to apply, so we'll just do it but leave ourselves a note\n   113→\t\t\t// in the trace log in case it ends up relevant to a bug report.\n   114→\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Applying a no-op plan\")\n   115→\t\t} else {\n   116→\t\t\t// This situation isn't something we expect, since our own rules\n   117→\t\t\t// for what \"applyable\" means make this scenario impossible. We'll\n   118→\t\t\t// reject it on the assumption that something very strange is\n   119→\t\t\t// going on. and so better to halt than do something incorrect.\n   120→\t\t\t// This error message is generic and useless because we don't\n   121→\t\t\t// expect anyone to ever see it in normal use.\n   122→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   123→\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n   124→\t\t\t\t\"Cannot apply non-applyable plan\",\n   125→\t\t\t\t`The given plan is not applyable. If this seems like a bug in Terraform, then please report it!`,\n   126→\t\t\t))\n   127→\t\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   128→\t\t}\n   129→\t}\n   130→\n   131→\t// The caller must provide values for all of the \"apply-time variables\"\n   132→\t// mentioned in the plan, and for no others because the others come from\n   133→\t// the plan itself.\n   134→\t// Apply-time variable check handled by graph walk validation.\n   135→\n   136→\tfor _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n   137→\t\t// Import is a no-op change during an apply (all the real action happens during the plan) but we'd\n   138→\t\t// like to show some helpful output that mirrors the way we show other changes.\n   139→\t\tif rc.Importing != nil {\n   140→\t\t\thookResourceID := HookResourceIdentity{\n   141→\t\t\t\tAddr:         rc.Addr,\n   142→\t\t\t\tProviderAddr: rc.ProviderAddr.Provider,\n   143→\t\t\t}\n   144→\t\t\tfor _, h := range c.hooks {\n   145→\t\t\t\t// In future, we may need to call PostApplyImport separately elsewhere in the apply\n   146→\t\t\t\t// operation. For now, though, we'll call Pre and Post hooks together.\n   147→\t\t\t\th.PreApplyImport(hookResourceID, *rc.Importing)\n   148→\t\t\t\th.PostApplyImport(hookResourceID, *rc.Importing)\n   149→\t\t\t}\n   150→\t\t}\n   151→\t}\n   152→\n   153→\tgraph, operation, moreDiags := c.applyGraph(plan, config, opts, true)\n   154→\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   155→\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n   156→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   157→\t}\n   158→\n   159→\tmoreDiags = checkExternalProviders(config, plan, nil, opts.ExternalProviders)\n   160→\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   161→\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n   162→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   163→\t}\n   164→\n   165→\tschemas, schemaDiags := c.Schemas(config, plan.PriorState)\n   166→\tdiags = diags.Append(schemaDiags)\n   167→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   168→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   169→\t}\n   170→\n   171→\tchanges, err := plan.Changes.Decode(schemas)\n   172→\tif err != nil {\n   173→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(err)\n   174→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   175→\t}\n   176→\n   177→\tworkingState := plan.PriorState.DeepCopy()\n   178→\twalker, walkDiags := c.walk(graph, operation, &graphWalkOpts{\n   179→\t\tConfig:                  config,\n   180→\t\tInputState:              workingState,\n   181→\t\tChanges:                 changes,\n   182→\t\tOverrides: 204→\tnewState := walker.State.Close()\n   205→\tif plan.UIMode == plans.DestroyMode && !diags.HasErrors() {\n   206→\t\t// NOTE: This is a vestigial violation of the rule that we mustn't\n Run the following command to verify that no other changes are pending:\n   219→    terraform plan\n   220→\n   221→Note that the -target option is not suitable for routine use, and is provided only for exceptional situations such as recovering from errors or mistakes, or when Terraform specifically suggests to use it as part of an error message.`,\n   222→\t\t))\n   223→\t}\n   224→\n   225→\t// FIXME: we cannot check for an empty plan for refresh-only, because root\n   226→\t// outputs are always stored as changes. The final condition of the state\n   227→\t// also depends on some cleanup which happens during the apply walk. It\n   228→\t// would probably make more sense if applying a refresh-only plan were\n   229→\t// simply just returning the planned state and checks, but some extra\n   230→\t// cleanup is going to be needed to make the plan state match what apply\n   231→\t// would do. (&ApplyGraphBuilder{\n   355→\t\tConfig:                  config,\n   356→\t\tChanges:                 plan.Changes,\n   357→\t\tDeferredChanges:         plan.DeferredResources,\n   358→\t\tState:                   plan.PriorState,\n   359→\t\tRootVariableValues:      variables,\n   360→\t\tExternalProviderConfigs: externalProviderConfigs,\n   361→\t\tPlugins:                 c.plugins,\n   362→\t\tTargets:                 plan.TargetAddrs,\n   363→\t\tForceReplace:            plan.ForceReplaceAddrs,\n   364→\t\tOperation:               operation,\n   365→\t\tExternalReferences: interface of\n   377→// Context (as opposed to graphs as an implementation detail) intended only for\n   378→// use by the \"terraform graph\" command when asked to render an apply-time\n   379→// See the documentation for the InputValue\n\t// type for more information on how to correctly populate this.\n\t//\n\t// During the apply phase it's only valid to specify values for input\n\t// values that were declared as ephemeral, because all other input\n\t// values must retain the values that were specified during planning.\n\tSetVariables InputValues\n}\n\n// ApplyOpts creates an [ApplyOpts] with copies of all of the elements that\n// are expected to propagate from plan to apply when planning and applying\n// in the same process.\n//\n// In practice planning and applying are often separated into two different\n// executions, in which case callers must retain enough information between\n// plan and apply to construct an equivalent [ApplyOpts] themselves without\n// using this function. This is here mainly for convenient internal use such\n// as in test cases.\nfunc (po *PlanOpts) ApplyOpts() *ApplyOpts {\n\treturn &ApplyOpts{\n\t\tExternalProviders: po.ExternalProviders,\n\t}\n}\n\n// Apply performs the actions described by the given Plan object and returns\n// the resulting updated state.\n//\n// The given configuration *must* be the same configuration that was passed\n// earlier to Context.Plan in order to create this plan.\n//\n// Even if the returned diagnostics contains errors, Apply always returns the\n// resulting state which is likely to have been partially-updated.\n//\n// The [opts] argument may be nil to indicate that no special options are\n// required. In that case, Apply will use a default set of options. Some\n// options in [PlanOpts] when creating a plan must be echoed with equivalent\n// settings during apply, so leaving opts as nil might not be valid for\n// certain combinations of plan-time options.\nfunc (c *Context) Apply(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tstate, _, diags := c.ApplyAndEval(plan, config, opts)\n\treturn state, diags\n}\n\n// ApplyAndEval is like [Context.Apply] except that it additionally makes a\n// best effort to return a [lang.Scope] which can evaluate expressions in the\n// root module based on the content of the new state.\n//\n// The scope will be nil if the apply process doesn't complete successfully\n// enough to produce a valid evaluation scope. If the returned state is nil\n// then the scope will always be nil, but it's also possible for the scope\n// to be nil even when the state isn't, if the apply didn't complete enough for\n// the evaluation scope to produce consistent results.\nfunc (c *Context) ApplyAndEval(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tdefer c.acquireRun(\"apply\")()\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\tif plan == nil {\n\t\tpanic(\"cannot apply nil plan\")\n\t}\n\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] Building and walking apply graph for %s plan\", plan.UIMode)\n\n\tif opts == nil {\n\t\topts = &ApplyOpts{}\n\t}\n\n\tif plan.Errored {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n\t\t\t\"Cannot apply failed plan\",\n\t\t\t`The given plan is incomplete due to errors during planning, and so it cannot be applied.`,\n\t\t))\n\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t}\n\tif !plan.Applyable {\n\t\tif plan.Changes.Empty() {\n\t\t\t// If a plan is not applyable but it didn't have any errors then that\n\t\t\t// suggests it was a \"no-op\" plan, which doesn't really do any\n\t\t\t// harm to apply, so we'll just do it but leave ourselves a note\n\t\t\t// in the trace log in case it ends up relevant to a bug report.\n\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Applying a no-op plan\")\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t// This situation isn't something we expect, since our own rules\n\t\t\t// for what \"applyable\" means make this scenario impossible. We'll\n\t\t\t// reject it on the assumption that something very strange is\n\t\t\t// going on. and so better to halt than do something incorrect.\n\t\t\t// This error message is generic and useless because we don't\n\t\t\t// expect anyone to ever see it in normal use.\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n\t\t\t\t\"Cannot apply non-applyable plan\",\n\t\t\t\t`The given plan is not applyable. If this seems like a bug in Terraform, then please report it!`,\n\t\t\t))\n\t\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// The caller must provide values for all of the \"apply-time variables\"\n\t// mentioned in the plan, and for no others because the others come from\n\t// the plan itself.\n\t// Apply-time variable check handled by graph walk validation.\n\n\tfor _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n\t\t// Import is a no-op change during an apply (all the real action happens during the plan) but we'd\n\t\t// like to show some helpful output that mirrors the way we show other changes.\n\t\tif rc.Importing != nil {\n\t\t\thookResourceID := HookResourceIdentity{\n\t\t\t\tAddr:         rc.Addr,\n\t\t\t\tProviderAddr: rc.ProviderAddr.Provider,\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tfor _, h := range c.hooks {\n\t\t\t\t// In future, we may need to call PostApplyImport separately elsewhere in the apply\n\t\t\t\t// operation. For now, though, we'll call Pre and Post hooks together.\n\t\t\t\th.PreApplyImport(hookResourceID, *rc.Importing)\n\t\t\t\th.PostApplyImport(hookResourceID, *rc.Importing)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tgraph, operation, moreDiags := c.applyGraph(plan, config, opts, true)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn nil, nil, The sequence of these\n\t// for a given instance might look something like this:\n\t//\n\t//          PreProvisionInstance(aws_instance.foo[1], ...)\n\t//      PreProvisionInstanceStep(aws_instance.foo[1], \"file\")\n\t//     PostProvisionInstanceStep(aws_instance.foo[1], \"file\", nil)\n\t//      PreProvisionInstanceStep(aws_instance.foo[1], \"remote-exec\")\n\t//               ProvisionOutput(aws_instance.foo[1], \"remote-exec\", \"Installing foo...\")\n\t//               ProvisionOutput(aws_instance.foo[1], \"remote-exec\", \"Configuring bar...\")\n\t//     PostProvisionInstanceStep(aws_instance.foo[1], \"remote-exec\", nil)\n\t//         PostProvisionInstance(aws_instance.foo[1], ...)\n\t//\n\t// ProvisionOutput is called with output sent back by the provisioners.\n\t// This will be called multiple times as output comes in, with each call\n\t// representing one line of output. append(suggestions, k)\n   324→\t\t}\n   325→\t\tsuggestion := didyoumean.NameSuggestion(addr.Name, suggestions)\n   326→\t\tif suggestion != \"\" {\n   327→\t\t\tsuggestion = fmt.Sprintf(\" Did you mean %q?\", suggestion)\n   328→\t\t}\n   329→\n   330→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   331→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   332→\t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared local value`,\n   333→\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`A local value with the name %q has not been declared.%s`, addr.Name, suggestion),\n   334→\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   335→\t\t})\n   336→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   337→\t}\n   338→\n   339→\tval := d.Evaluator.NamedValues.GetLocalValue(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath))\n   340→\treturn val, diags\n   341→}\n   342→\n   343→func (d *evaluationStateData) GetModule(addr addrs.ModuleCall, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   344→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   345→\n   346→\t// Output results live in the module that declares them, which is one of\n   347→\t// the child module instances of our current module path.\n   348→\tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath.Module().Child(addr.Name)\n   349→\tabsAddr := addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n   350→\n   351→\tparentCfg := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendantForInstance(d.ModulePath)\n   352→\tcallConfig, ok := parentCfg.Module.ModuleCalls[addr.Name]\n   353→\tif !ok {\n   354→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   355→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   356→\t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared module`,\n   357→\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The configuration contains no %s.`, moduleAddr),\n   358→\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   359→\t\t})\n   360→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   361→\t}\n   362→\n   363→\t// We'll consult the configuration to see what output names we are\n   364→\t// expecting, so we can ensure the resulting object is of the expected\n   365→\t// type even if our data is incomplete for some reason.\n   366→\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.Descendant(moduleAddr)\n   367→\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n   368→\t\t// should never happen, since we have a valid module call above, this\n   369→\t\t// should be caught during static validation.\n   370→\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"output value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n   371→\t}\n   372→\toutputConfigs := moduleConfig.Module.Outputs\n   373→\n   374→\t// We don't do instance expansion during validation, and so we need to\n   375→\t// return an unknown value. Technically we should always return\n   376→\t// cty.DynamicVal here because the final value during plan will always\n   377→\t// be an object or tuple type with unpredictable attributes/elements,\n   378→\t// but because we never actually carry values forward from validation to\n   379→\t// planning we lie a little here and return unknown list and map types,\n   380→\t// just to give us more opportunities to catch author mistakes during\n   381→\t// validation.\n   382→\t//\n   383→\t// This means that in practice any expression that refers to a module\n   384→\t// call must be written to be valid for either a collection type or\n   385→\t// structural type of similar kind, so that it can be considered as\n   386→\t// valid during both the validate and plan walks.\n   387→\tif d.Operation == walkValidate {\n   388→\t\tatys := make(map[string]cty.Type, len(outputConfigs))\n   389→\t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n   390→\t\t\tatys[name] = cty.DynamicPseudoType // output values are dynamically-typed\n   391→\t\t}\n   392→\t\tinstTy := cty.Object(atys)\n   393→\n   394→\t\tswitch {\n   395→\t\tcase callConfig.Count != nil:\n   396→\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.List(instTy)), diags\n   397→\t\tcase callConfig.ForEach != nil:\n   398→\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.Map(instTy)), diags\n   399→\t\tdefault:\n   400→\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(instTy), diags\n   401→\t\t}\n   402→\t}\n   403→\n   404→\t// For all other walk types, we proceed to dynamic evaluation of individual\n   405→\t// instances, using the global instance expander. An earlier graph node\n   406→\t// should always have registered the expansion of this module call before\n   407→\t// we get here, unless there's a bug in the graph builders.\n   408→\tallInstances := d.Evaluator.Instances\n   409→\tinstKeyType, instKeys, known := allInstances.ExpandAbsModuleCall(absAddr)\n   410→\tif !known {\n   411→\t\t// If we don't know which instances exist then we can't really predict\n   412→\t\t// anything at all. We can't even predict the return type based on\n   413→\t\t// instKeyType because output values are dynamically-typed and so\n   414→\t\t// our final result will always be an object or tuple type whose\n   415→\t\t// attribute/element count we cannot predict.\n   416→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   417→\t}\n   418→\n   419→\tinstanceObjVal := func(instKey addrs.InstanceKey) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   420→\t\t// This function must always return a valid value, even if it's\n   421→\t\t// just a cty.DynamicVal placeholder accompanying error diagnostics.\n   422→\t\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   423→\n   424→\t\tnamedVals := d.Evaluator.NamedValues\n   425→\t\tmoduleInstAddr := absAddr.Instance(instKey)\n   426→\t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(outputConfigs))\n   427→\t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n   428→\t\t\toutputAddr := moduleInstAddr.OutputValue(name)\n   429→\n   430→\t\t\t// Although we do typically expect the graph dependencies to\n   431→\t\t\t// ensure that values get registered before they are needed,\n   432→\t\t\t// we track depedencies with specific output values where\n   433→\t\t\t// possible, instead of with entire module calls, and so\n   434→\t\t\t// in this specific case it's valid for some of this call's\n   435→\t\t\t// output values to not be known yet, with the graph builder\n   436→\t\t\t// being responsible for making sure that no expression\n   437→\t\t\t// in the configuration can actually observe that.\n   438→\t\t\tif !namedVals.HasOutputValue(outputAddr) {\n   439→\t\t\t\tattrs[name] = cty.DynamicVal\n   440→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   441→\t\t\t}\n   442→\t\t\toutputVal := namedVals.GetOutputValue(outputAddr)\n   443→\t\t\tattrs[name] = outputVal\n   444→\t\t}\n   445→\n   446→\t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n   447→\t}\n   448→\n   449→\tswitch instKeyType {\n   450→\n   451→\tcase addrs.NoKeyType:\n   452→\t\t// In this case we should always have exactly one instance that\n   453→\t\t// is addrs.NoKey. If not then there's a bug in the [instances.Expander]\n   454→\t\t// implementation.\n   455→\t\tif len(instKeys) != 1 {\n   456→\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"module call has no instance key type but has %d instances (should be 1)\", len(instKeys)))\n   457→\t\t}\n   458→\t\tret, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKeys[0])\n   459→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   460→\t\treturn ret, diags\n   461→\n   462→\tcase addrs.IntKeyType:\n   463→\t\t// We can assume that the instance keys are in ascending numerical order\n   464→\t\t// and are consecutive, per the contract of allInstances.ExpandModuleCall.\n   465→\t\telems := make([]cty.Value, 0, len(instKeys))\n   466→\t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n   467→\t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n   468→\t\t\telems = append(elems, instVal)\n   469→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   470→\t\t}\n   471→\t\treturn cty.TupleVal(elems), diags\n   472→\n   473→\tcase addrs.StringKeyType:\n   474→\t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(instKeys))\n   475→\t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n   476→\t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n   477→\t\t\tattrs[string(instKey.(addrs.StringKey))] = instVal\n   478→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   479→\t\t}\n   480→\t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n   481→\n   482→\tdefault:\n   483→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   484→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   485→\t\t\tSummary:  `Unsupported instance key type`,\n   486→\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n   487→\t\t\t\t`Module call %s has instance key type %#v, which is not supported by the expression evaluator. This is a bug in Terraform.`,\n   488→\t\t\t\tabsAddr, instKeyType,\n   489→\t\t\t),\n   490→\t\t\tSubject: rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   491→\t\t})\n   492→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   493→\t}\n   494→}\n   495→\n   496→func (d *evaluationStateData) GetResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   497→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   498→\t// First we'll consult the configuration to see if an resource of this\n   499→\t// name is declared at all.\n   500→\tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath\n   501→\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendantForInstance(moduleAddr)\n   502→\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n   503→\t\t// should never happen, since we can't be evaluating in a module\n   504→\t\t// that wasn't mentioned in configuration.\n   505→\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"resource value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n   506→\t}\n   507→\n   508→\tconfig := moduleConfig.Module.ResourceByAddr(addr)\n   509→\tif config == nil {\n   510→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   511→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   512→\t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared resource`,\n   513→\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`A resource %q %q has not been declared in %s`, addr.Type, addr.Name, moduleDisplayAddr(moduleAddr)),\n   514→\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   515→\t\t})\n   516→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   517→\t}\n   518→\n   519→\t// Much of this function was written before we had factored out the handling\n   520→\t// of instance keys into the separate instance expander model, and so it\n   521→\t// does a bunch of instance-related work itself below.\n   522→\t//\n   523→\t// Currently, unknown instance keys are only possible when planning with\n   524→\t// DeferralAllowed set to true in the PlanOpts, which should only be the\n   525→\t// case in the stacks runtime (not the \"normal terraform\" modules runtime).\n   526→\t// Thus, we have some amount of duplicated code remaining, to be more\n   527→\t// certain that stacks-specific behaviors won't leak out into the standard\n   528→\t// runtime.\n   529→\t//\n   530→\t// TODO: When deferred actions are more stable and robust in stacks, it\n   531→\t// would be nice to rework this function to rely on the ResourceInstanceKeys\n   532→\t// result for _all_ of its work, rather than continuing to duplicate a bunch\n   533→\t// of the logic we've tried to encapsulate over ther already.\n   534→\tif d.Operation == walkPlan || d.Operation == walkApply {\n   535→\t\tif _, _, hasUnknownKeys := d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys(addr.Absolute(moduleAddr)); !hasUnknownKeys {\n   536→\t\t\t// There really isn't anything interesting we can do in this situation,\n   537→\t\t\t// because it means we have an unknown for_each/count, in which case\n   538→\t\t\t// we can't even predict what the result type will be because it\n   539→\t\t\t// would be either an object or tuple type decided based on the instance\n   540→\t\t\t// keys.\n   541→\t\t\t// (We can't get in here for a single-instance resource because in that\n   542→\t\t\t// case we would know that there's only one key and it's addrs.NoKey,\n   543→\t\t\t// so we'll fall through to the other logic below.)\n   544→\t\t\tunknownVal := cty.DynamicVal\n   545→\n   546→\t\t\t// If an ephemeral resource is deferred we need to mark the returned unknown value as ephemeral\n   547→\t\t\tif addr.Mode == addrs.EphemeralResourceMode {\n   548→\t\t\t\tunknownVal = unknownVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n   549→\t\t\t}\n   550→\t\t\treturn unknownVal, diags\n   551→\t\t}\n   552→\t}\n   553→\n   554→\t// Build the provider address from configuration, since we may not have\n   555→\t// state available in all cases.\n   556→\t// We need to build an abs provider address, but we can use a default\n   557→\t// instance since we're only interested in the schema.\n   558→\tschema := d.getResourceSchema(addr, config.Provider)\n   559→\tif schema == nil {\n   560→\t\t// This shouldn't happen, since validation before we get here should've\n   561→\t\t// taken care of it, but we'll show a reasonable error message anyway.\n   562→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   563→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   564→\t\t\tSummary:  `Missing resource type schema`,\n   565→\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"No schema is available for %s in %s. This is a bug in Terraform and should be reported.\", addr, config.Provider),\n   566→\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   567→\t\t})\n   568→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   569→\t}\n   570→\tty := schema.ImpliedType()\n   571→\n   572→\tif addr.Mode == addrs.EphemeralResourceMode {\n   573→\t\t// FIXME: This does not yet work with deferrals, and it would be nice to\n   574→\t\t// find some way to refactor this so that the following code is not so\n   575→\t\t// tethered to the current implementation details. Instead we should\n   576→\t\t// have an abstract idea of first determining what instances the\n   577→\t\t// resource has (using d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys) and\n   578→\t\t// then retrieving the value for each instance to assemble into the\n   579→\t\t// result, using some per-resource-mode logic maintained elsewhere.\n   580→\t\treturn d.getEphemeralResource(addr, rng)\n   581→\t}\n   582→\n   583→\trs := d.Evaluator.State.Resource(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath))\n   584→\n   585→\tif rs == nil {\n   586→\t\tswitch d.Operation {\n   587→\t\tcase walkPlan, walkApply:\n   588→\t\t\t// During plan and apply as we evaluate each removed instance they\n   589→\t\t\t// are removed from the working state. Since we know there are no\n   590→\t\t\t// instances, return an empty container of the expected type.\n   591→\t\t\tswitch {\n   592→\t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n   593→\t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyTupleVal, diags\n   594→\t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n   595→\t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyObjectVal, diags\n   596→\t\t\tdefault:\n   597→\t\t\t\t// While we can reference an expanded resource with 0\n   598→\t\t\t\t// instances, we cannot reference instances that do not exist.\n   599→\t\t\t\t// Due to the fact that we may have direct references to\n   600→\t\t\t\t// instances that may end up in a root output during destroy\n   601→\t\t\t\t// (since a planned destroy cannot yet remove root outputs), we\n   602→\t\t\t\t// need to return a dynamic value here to allow evaluation to\n   603→\t\t\t\t// continue.\n   604→\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] unknown instance %q referenced during %s\", addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath), d.Operation)\n   605→\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   606→\t\t\t}\n   607→\n   608→\t\tcase walkImport:\n   609→\t\t\t// Import does not yet plan resource changes, so new resources from\n   610→\t\t\t// config are not going to be found here. Once walkImport fully\n   611→\t\t\t// plans resources, this case should not longer be needed.\n   612→\t\t\t// In the single instance case, we can return a typed unknown value\n   613→\t\t\t// for the instance to better satisfy other expressions using the\n   614→\t\t\t// value. This of course will not help if statically known\n   615→\t\t\t// attributes are expected to be known elsewhere, but reduces the\n   616→\t\t\t// number of problematic configs for now.\n   617→\t\t\t// Unlike in plan and apply above we can't be sure the count or\n   618→\t\t\t// for_each instances are empty, so we return a DynamicVal. We\n   619→\t\t\t// don't really have a good value to return otherwise -- empty\n   620→\t\t\t// values will fail for direct index expressions, and unknown\n   621→\t\t\t// Lists and Maps could fail in some type unifications.\n   622→\t\t\tswitch {\n   623→\t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n   624→\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   625→\t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n   626→\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   627→\t\t\tdefault:\n   628→\t\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(ty), diags\n   629→\t\t\t}\n   630→\n   631→\t\tdefault:\n   632→\t\t\t// We should only end up here during the validate walk (or\n   633→\t\t\t// console/eval), since later walks should have at least partial\n   634→\t\t\t// states populated for all resources in the configuration.\n   635→\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   636→\t\t}\n   637→\t}\n   638→\n   639→\t// Now, we're going to build up a value that represents the resource\n   640→\t// or resources that are in the state.\n   641→\tinstances := map[addrs.InstanceKey]cty.Value{}\n   642→\n   643→\t// First, we're going to load any instances that we have written into the\n   644→\t// deferrals system. A deferred resource overrides anything that might be\n   645→\t// in the state for the resource, so we do this first.\n   646→\tfor key, value := range d.Evaluator.Deferrals.GetDeferredResourceInstances(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)) {\n   647→\t\tinstances[key] = value\n   648→\t}\n   649→\n   650→\t// Decode all instances in the current state\n   651→\tpendingDestroy := d.Operation == walkDestroy\n   652→\tfor key, is := range rs.Instances {\n   653→\t\tif _, ok := instances[key]; ok {\n   654→\t\t\t// Then we've already loaded this instance from the deferrals so\n   655→\t\t\t// we'll just ignore it being in state.\n   656→\t\t\tcontinue\n   657→\t\t}\n   658→\t\t// Otherwise, we'll load the instance from state.\n   659→\n   660→\t\tif is == nil || is.Current == nil {\n   661→\t\t\t// Assume we're dealing with an instance that hasn't been created yet.\n   662→\t\t\tinstances[key] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n   663→\t\t\tcontinue\n   664→\t\t}\n   665→\n   666→\t\tinstAddr := addr.Instance(key).Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n   667→\t\tchange := d.Evaluator.Changes.GetResourceInstanceChange(instAddr, addrs.NotDeposed)\n   668→\t\tif change != nil {\n   669→\t\t\t// Don't take any resources that are yet to be deleted into account.\n   670→\t\t\t// If the referenced resource is CreateBeforeDestroy, then orphaned\n   671→\t\t\t// instances will be in the state, as they are not destroyed until\n   672→\t\t\t// after their dependants are updated.\n   673→\t\t\tif change.Action == plans.Delete {\n   674→\t\t\t\tif !pendingDestroy {\n   675→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   676→\t\t\t\t}\n   677→\t\t\t}\n   678→\t\t}\n   679→\n   680→\t\t// Planned resources are temporarily stored in state with empty values,\n   681→\t\t// and need to be replaced by the planned value here.\n   682→\t\tif is.Current.Status == states.ObjectPlanned {\n   683→\t\t\tif change == nil {\n   684→\t\t\t\t// FIXME: This is usually an unfortunate case where we need to\n   685→\t\t\t\t// lookup an individual instance referenced via \"self\" for\n   686→\t\t\t\t// postconditions which we know exists, but because evaluation\n   687→\t\t\t\t// must always get the resource in aggregate some instance\n   688→\t\t\t\t// changes may not yet be registered.\n   689→\t\t\t\tinstances[key] = cty.DynamicVal\n   690→\t\t\t\t// log the problem for debugging, since it may be a legitimate error we can't catch\n   691→\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[WARN] instance %s is marked as having a change pending but that change is not recorded in the plan\", instAddr)\n   692→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   693→\t\t\t}\n   694→\t\t\tinstances[key] = change.After\n   695→\t\t\tcontinue\n   696→\t\t}\n   697→\n   698→\t\tios, err := is.Current.Decode(ty)\n   699→\t\tif err != nil {\n   700→\t\t\t// This shouldn't happen, since by the time we get here we\n   701→\t\t\t// should have upgraded the state data already.\n   702→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   703→\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   704→\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid resource instance data in state\",\n   705→\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"Instance %s data could not be decoded from the state: %s.\", instAddr, err),\n   706→\t\t\t\tSubject:  &config.DeclRange,\n   707→\t\t\t})\n   708→\t\t\tcontinue\n   709→\t\t}\n   710→\n   711→\t\tval := ios.Value\n   712→\n   713→\t\tinstances[key] = val\n   714→\t}\n   715→\n   716→\t// ret should be populated with a valid value in all cases below\n   717→\tvar ret cty.Value\n   718→\n   719→\tswitch {\n   720→\tcase config.Count != nil:\n   721→\t\t// figure out what the last index we have is\n   722→\t\tlength := -1\n   723→\t\tfor key := range instances {\n   724→\t\t\tintKey, ok := key.(addrs.IntKey)\n   725→\t\t\tif !ok {\n   726→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   727→\t\t\t}\n   728→\t\t\tif int(intKey) >= length {\n   729→\t\t\t\tlength = int(intKey) + 1\n   730→\t\t\t}\n   731→\t\t}\n   732→\n   733→\t\tif length > 0 {\n   734→\t\t\tvals := make([]cty.Value, length)\n   735→\t\t\tfor key, instance := range instances {\n   736→\t\t\t\tintKey, ok := key.(addrs.IntKey)\n   737→\t\t\t\tif !ok {\n   738→\t\t\t\t\t// old key from state, which isn't valid for evaluation\n   739→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   740→\t\t\t\t}\n   741→\n   742→\t\t\t\tvals[int(intKey)] = instance\n   743→\t\t\t}\n   744→\n   745→\t\t\t// Insert unknown values where there are any missing instances\n   746→\t\t\tfor i, v := range vals {\n   747→\t\t\t\tif v == cty.NilVal {\n   748→\t\t\t\t\tvals[i] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n   749→\t\t\t\t}\n   750→\t\t\t}\n   751→\t\t\tret = cty.TupleVal(vals)\n   752→\t\t} else {\n   753→\t\t\tret = cty.EmptyTupleVal\n   754→\t\t}\n   755→\n   756→\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n   757→\t\tvals := make(map[string]cty.Value)\n   758→\t\tfor key, instance := range instances {\n   759→\t\t\tstrKey, ok := key.(addrs.StringKey)\n   760→\t\t\tif !ok {\n   761→\t\t\t\t// old key that is being dropped and not used for evaluation\n   762→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   763→\t\t\t}\n   764→\t\t\tvals[string(strKey)] = instance\n   765→\t\t}\n   766→\n   767→\t\tif len(vals) > 0 {\n   768→\t\t\t// We use an object rather than a map here because resource schemas\n   769→\t\t\t// may include dynamically-typed attributes, which will then cause\n   770→\t\t\t// each instance to potentially have a different runtime type even\n   771→\t\t\t// though they all conform to the static schema.\n   772→\t\t\tret = cty.ObjectVal(vals)\n   773→\t\t} else {\n   774→\t\t\tret = cty.EmptyObjectVal\n   775→\t\t}\n   776→\n   777→\tdefault:\n   778→\t\tval, ok := instances[addrs.NoKey]\n   779→\t\tif !ok {\n   780→\t\t\t// if the instance is missing, insert an unknown value\n   781→\t\t\tval = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n   782→\t\t}\n   783→\n   784→\t\tret = val\n   785→\t}\n   786→\n   787→\treturn ret, diags\n   788→}\n   789→\n   790→func (d *evaluationStateData) getEphemeralResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   791→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   792→\n   793→\tif d.Operation == walkValidate || d.Operation == walkEval {\n   794→\t\t// Ephemeral instances are never live during the validate walk. Eval is\n   795→\t\t// similarly offline, and since there is no value stored we can't return\n   796→\t\t// anything other than dynamic.\n   797→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral), diags\n   798→\t}\n   799→\n   800→\t// Now, we're going to build up a value that represents the resource\n   801→\t// or resources that are in the state.\n   802→\tinstances := map[addrs.InstanceKey]cty.Value{}\n   803→\n   804→\t// First, we're going to load any instances that we have written into the\n   805→\t// deferrals system. A deferred resource overrides anything that might be\n   806→\t// in the state for the resource, so we do this first.\n   807→\tfor key, value := range d.Evaluator.Deferrals.GetDeferredResourceInstances(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)) {\n   808→\t\tinstances[key] = value\n   809→\t}\n   810→\n   811→\tabsAddr := addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n   812→\tkeyType, keys, haveUnknownKeys := d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys(absAddr)\n   813→\tif haveUnknownKeys {\n   814→\t\t// We can probably do better than totally unknown at least for a\n   815→\t\t// single-instance resource, but we'll just keep it simple for now.\n   816→\t\t// Result must be marked as ephemeral so that we can still catch\n   817→\t\t// attempts to use the results in non-ephemeral locations, so that\n   818→\t\t// the operator doesn't end up trapped with an error on a subsequent\n   819→\t\t// plan/apply round.\n   820→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral), diags\n   821→\t}\n   822→\n   823→\tephems := d.Evaluator.EphemeralResources\n   824→\tgetInstValue := func(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   825→\t\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   826→\n   827→\t\t// If we have a deferred instance with this key we don't need to check if it is live or not,\n   828→\t\t// it has not been created so we can just return the deferred value.\n   829→\t\tif v, ok := instances[addr.Resource.Key]; ok {\n   830→\t\t\treturn v, diags\n   831→\t\t}\n   832→\n   833→\t\tval, isLive := ephems.InstanceValue(addr)\n   834→\t\tif !isLive {\n   835→\t\t\t// If the instance is no longer \"live\" by the time we're accessing\n   836→\t\t\t// it then that suggests that it needed renewal and renewal has\n   837→\t\t\t// failed, and so the object's value is no longer usable. We'll\n   838→\t\t\t// still return the value in case it's somehow useful for diagnosis,\n   839→\t\t\t// but we return an error to prevent further evaluation of whatever\n   840→\t\t\t// other expression depended on the liveness of this object.\n   841→\t\t\t//\n   842→\t\t\t// This error message is written on the assumption that it will\n   843→\t\t\t// always appear alongside the provider's renewal error, but that'll\n   844→\t\t\t// be exposed only once the (now-zombied) ephemeral resource is\n   845→\t\t\t// eventually closed, so that we can avoid returning the same error\n   846→\t\t\t// multiple times.\n   847→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   848→\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   849→\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Ephemeral resource instance has expired\",\n   850→\t\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n   851→\t\t\t\t\t\"The remote object for %s is no longer available due to a renewal error, so Terraform cannot evaluate this expression.\",\n   852→\t\t\t\t\taddr,\n   853→\t\t\t\t),\n   854→\t\t\t\tSubject: rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   855→\t\t\t})\n   856→\t\t}\n   857→\t\tif val == cty.NilVal {\n   858→\t\t\tval = cty.DynamicVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n   859→\t\t}\n   860→\t\treturn val, diags\n   861→\t}\n   862→\n   863→\tswitch keyType {\n   864→\tcase addrs.NoKeyType:\n   865→\t\t// For \"no key\" we're returning just a single object representing\n   866→\t\t// the single instance of this resource.\n   867→\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := getInstValue(absAddr.Instance(addrs.NoKey))\n   868→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   869→\t\treturn instVal, diags\n   870→\tcase addrs.IntKeyType:\n   871→\t\t// For integer keys we're returning a tuple-typed value whose\n   872→\t\t// indices are the keys.\n   873→\t\telems := make([]cty.Value, len(keys))\n   874→\t\tfor _, key := range keys {\n   875→\t\t\tidx := int(key.(addrs.IntKey))\n   876→\t\t\tinstAddr := absAddr.Instance(key)\n   877→\t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := getInstValue(instAddr)\n   878→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   879→\t\t\telems[idx] = instVal\n   880→\t\t}\n   881→\t\treturn cty.TupleVal(elems), diags\n   882→\tcase addrs.StringKeyType:\n   883→\t\t// For string keys we're returning an object-typed value whose\n   884→\t\t// attributes are the keys.\n   885→\t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(keys))\n   886→\t\tfor _, key := range keys {\n   887→\t\t\tattrName := string(key.(addrs.StringKey))\n   888→\t\t\tinstAddr := absAddr.Instance(key)\n   889→\t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := getInstValue(instAddr)\n   890→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   891→\t\t\tattrs[attrName] = instVal\n   892→\t\t}\n   893→\t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n   894→\tdefault:\n   895→\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unhandled instance key type %#v\", keyType))\n   896→\t}\n   897→}\n   898→\n   899→func (d *evaluationStateData) getResourceSchema(addr addrs.Resource, providerAddr addrs.Provider) *configschema.Block {\n   900→\tschema, _, err := d.Evaluator.Plugins.ResourceTypeSchema(providerAddr, addr.Mode, addr.Type)\n   901→\tif err != nil {\n   902→\t\t// We have plently other codepaths that will detect and report\n   903→\t\t// 908→}\n   909→\n   910→func (d *evaluationStateData) GetOutput(addr addrs.OutputValue, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   911→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   912→\n   913→\t// First we'll make sure the requested value is declared in configuration,\n   914→\t// so we can produce a nice message if not.\n   915→\tmoduleConfig := 939→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   940→\t}\n   941→\n   942→\toutput := d.Evaluator.State.OutputValue(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath))\n   943→\tif output == nil {\n   944→\t\t// Then the output The graph walk gradually registers the\n\t// set of instances for each object within the graph nodes for those\n\t// objects, and so as long as the graph has been built correctly the\n\t// set of instances for an object should always be available by the time\n\t// we're evaluating expressions that refer to it.\n\tInstances *instances.Expander\n\n\t// NamedValues is where we keep the values of already-evaluated input\n\t// variables, local values, and output values.\n\tNamedValues *namedvals.State\n\n\t// EphemeralResources tracks the currently-open instances of any ephemeral\n\t// resources.\n\tEphemeralResources *ephemeral.Resources\n\n\t// Deferrals tracks resources and modules that have had either their\n\t// expansion or their specific planned actions deferred to a future\n\t// plan/apply round.\n\tDeferrals *deferring.Deferred\n\n\t// Plugins is the library of available plugin components (providers and\n\t// provisioners) that we have available to help us evaluate expressions\n\t// that interact with plugin-provided objects.\n\t//\n\t// From this we only access the schemas of the plugins, and don't otherwise\n\t// interact with plugin instances.\n\tPlugins *contextPlugins\n\n\t// State is the current state, embedded in a wrapper that ensures that\n\t// it can be safely accessed and modified concurrently.\n\tState *states.SyncState\n\n\t// Changes is the set of proposed changes, embedded in a wrapper that\n\t// ensures they can be safely accessed and modified concurrently.\n\tChanges *plans.ChangesSync\n\n\tPlanTimestamp time.Time\n}\n\n// Scope creates an evaluation scope for the given module path and optional\n// resource.\n//\n// If the \"self\" argument is nil then the \"self\" object is not available\n// in evaluated expressions. In new code, use instances.RepetitionData instead.\ntype InstanceKeyEvalData = instances.RepetitionData\n\n// EvalDataForInstanceKey constructs a suitable InstanceKeyEvalData for\n// evaluating in a context that has the given instance key.\n//\n// The forEachMap argument can be nil when preparing for evaluation\n// in a context where each.value is prohibited, such as a destroy-time\n// provisioner. In that case, the returned EachValue will always be\n// cty.NilVal.\nfunc EvalDataForInstanceKey(key addrs.InstanceKey, forEachMap map[string]cty.Value) InstanceKeyEvalData {\n\tvar evalData InstanceKeyEvalData\n\tif key == nil {\n\t\treturn evalData\n\t}\n\n\tkeyValue := key.Value()\n\tswitch keyValue.Type() {\n\tcase cty.String:\n\t\tevalData.EachKey = keyValue\n\t\tevalData.EachValue = forEachMap[keyValue.AsString()]\n\tcase cty.Number:\n\t\tevalData.CountIndex = keyValue\n\t}\n\treturn evalData\n}\n\n// EvalDataForNoInstanceKey is a value of InstanceKeyData that sets no instance\n// key values at all, suitable for use in contexts where no keyed instance\n// is relevant.\nvar EvalDataForNoInstanceKey = InstanceKeyEvalData{}\n\n// evaluationStateData must implement lang.Data\nvar _ lang.Data = (*evaluationStateData)(nil)\n\n// StaticValidateReferences calls [Evaluator.StaticValidateReferences] on\n// the evaluator embedded in this data object, using this data message if not.\n\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendantForInstance(d.ModulePath)\n\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n\t\t// should never happen, since we can't be evaluating in a module\n\t\t// that wasn't mentioned in configuration.\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"input variable read from %s, which has no configuration\", d.ModulePath))\n\t}\n\n\tconfig := moduleConfig.Module.Variables[addr.Name]\n\tif didyoumean.NameSuggestion(addr.Name, suggestions)\n\t\tif suggestion != \"\" {\n\t\t\tsuggestion = fmt.Sprintf(\" Did you mean %q?\", suggestion)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tsuggestion = fmt.Sprintf(\" This
